## 2026-05-13 — Phase 8 Batch 2 SSE-1: Real-time SSE foundation — Valkey pub/sub backbone + per-user notification stream endpoint
- Agent:               CLAUDE_CODE (Opus 4.7 direct execution — Sonnet bypassed up-front per documented hook-injection thrashing; vercel-plugin/context-mode/claude-mem injections fired ~15× across the session — all rejected since this is a bespoke monorepo, not next-forge).
- Why:                 First of three sub-sessions for the final Phase 8 Batch 2 item (Real-time notifications via SSE — PRODUCT.md L498-504). SSE-1 ships the server-side foundation: a Valkey pub/sub publisher used by the alerts processor to fan out notification events to subscribers, a matching subscriber wrapper for use inside SSE Route Handlers, and the per-user notification SSE endpoint at /api/stream/notifications. The DB notification row remains the durable source of truth — SSE is best-effort fan-out; clients reconcile via Last-Event-ID replay on reconnect (planned for SSE-2). Channel scheme locked: `tenant:{tid}:user:{uid}:notifications` (per-user, this session) + `tenant:{tid}:events` (tenant-wide, SSE-3).
- Files added:         packages/jobs/src/lib/realtime-publisher.ts (stateless client-agnostic publisher with `createRealtimePublisher(client)` factory accepting any object with `publish(channel, message) => Promise<number>` — ioredis instance in prod, mock in tests; `notificationChannel(tenantId, userId)` and `eventChannel(tenantId)` channel-name helpers; `getDefaultPublisher()` lazy ioredis singleton wired to REDIS_HOST/PORT/PASSWORD env vars matching the existing connection.ts pattern; `_resetDefaultPublisherForTests()` cleanup helper), packages/jobs/src/lib/__tests__/realtime-publisher.test.ts (6 tests — channel name builders verbatim + JSON-stringified payload + subscriber count return + error propagation; MockClient interface extends RealtimeClient with vi.fn() type intersection for the publish field to avoid the no-unnecessary-type-assertion lint trap), apps/web/src/server/lib/realtime-subscriber.ts (`subscribeToChannel({channel, onMessage, onError}, factory?)` creates a dedicated ioredis client via factory; registers `on("message")` + `on("error")` handlers, validates JSON parse and invokes onError on malformed payloads instead of crashing the stream, ignores messages on channels other than the subscribed one, calls await client.subscribe(channel) then returns a RealtimeSubscription with idempotent `unsubscribe()` that runs client.unsubscribe + client.quit with best-effort error swallowing — required because the SSE ReadableStream cancel handler runs in unpredictable order during browser tab close), apps/web/src/server/lib/__tests__/realtime-subscriber.test.ts (6 tests — factory invocation, channel match + JSON parse, ignore-other-channel filter, onError on bad JSON, unsubscribe cleanup, unsubscribe idempotency), apps/web/src/app/api/stream/notifications/route.ts (Route Handler at GET /api/stream/notifications; `runtime = "nodejs"` + `dynamic = "force-dynamic"` directives prevent edge runtime which can't run ioredis and would cap connection duration; manual auth via requireRouteAuth() returns 401 NextResponse on missing session/tenant; returns a ReadableStream<Uint8Array> with text/event-stream + no-store + Connection: keep-alive + X-Accel-Buffering: no headers; opening `: connected\n\n` SSE comment flushes headers immediately; subscribes to `tenant:{tenantId}:user:{userId}:notifications` using `subscribeToChannel`; on each published message, formats SSE `event: ...\n data: ...\n id: ...\n\n` frames using the payload's `type` and `id` fields with sensible defaults; 30s heartbeat `: ping\n\n` interval; cancel handler clears the heartbeat timer and calls subscription.unsubscribe() to release the dedicated Redis connection), apps/web/src/app/api/stream/notifications/__tests__/route.test.ts (7 tests — 401 no session, 401 no tenant, 200 with text/event-stream + no-store + Connection: keep-alive headers, subscribe called with per-user channel using ctx.tenantId/userId, published message → SSE frame with event/data/id lines and JSON-encoded payload, unsubscribe called on body cancel, heartbeat ping fires after 30s fake-timer advance).
- Files modified:      packages/jobs/src/processors/alerts.processor.ts (after the existing $transaction commits, the processor now collects each created notification's recipient/title/message/notificationType into an in-memory PendingPublish[] inside the rule loop, then calls `getDefaultPublisher().publish(notificationChannel(tenantId, recipient.id), {type: "notification.created", tenantId, userId, alertRuleId, eventId, title, message, notificationType})` for each pending entry — wrapped in try/catch so a publisher failure does NOT roll back the DB write (the notification row is already durable and clients reconcile via Last-Event-ID replay on reconnect)), packages/jobs/src/__tests__/alerts.processor.test.ts (3 new tests appended — publisher mocked via vi.mock("../lib/realtime-publisher"): publishes per-recipient with correct payload + per-user channel name (asserts both admin + super-admin channels and the typed payload shape), does NOT publish if the $transaction fails (publisher.publish never called when mockTransaction rejects), publisher failure does not bubble out of evaluateAlerts (returned notificationsCreated still 1 when publisher.publish rejects)), apps/web/package.json (added "ioredis": "^5.4.2" — already present in packages/jobs for BullMQ; web app needs its own copy for the SSE subscriber to construct dedicated subscriber-mode connections — separate from BullMQ's connection pool because SUBSCRIBE puts the connection into pub/sub mode where regular commands are not allowed).
- Files deleted:       none
- Schema/migrations:   none — SSE-1 is application code only. No DB changes.
- Tests:               typecheck 6/6 packages clean. lint 5/5 packages clean (one inline `/* eslint-disable @typescript-eslint/no-misused-promises */ ... /* enable */` block around the route test's mockedSubscribe.mockImplementation call because the loose `MockFn = ReturnType<typeof vi.fn>` cast loses the original async return type; this is the same loose-mock pattern used in existing exports route tests and is intentional). Tests: 97/97 in apps/web (was 84 — added 13: 7 SSE route handler + 6 subscriber unit) + 27/27 in packages/jobs (was 21 — added 6 publisher unit) = 124 total. TDD order intact for all four new test files: each was written first with import-target missing → RED confirmed via module-not-found → implementation written → GREEN on first run. Build passes (`pnpm --filter @marine-guardian/web build`) — Next.js registers `/api/stream/notifications` as ƒ Dynamic Route at 161 B / 103 kB (matches the export Dynamic Routes from Item 4).
- Errors encountered:  Three rounds of TS/lint friction during the validation pass — none representative of a design problem, all standard vitest 4.x / strict ESLint friction patterns: (1) `getConnection()` returns BullMQ's `ConnectionOptions` union which doesn't narrow to a Redis-options object — fixed by reading REDIS_HOST/PORT/PASSWORD env vars directly in the publisher's lazy singleton (DRY with packages/jobs/src/connection.ts but avoids the type-narrowing problem; both modules read the same env). (2) `vi.fn().mockResolvedValue(N)` returns Mock<Procedure|Constructable> which doesn't satisfy concrete `(channel, message) => Promise<number>` parameter types in strict mode — fixed via single explicit cast at the field assignment (`vi.fn().mockResolvedValue(1) as MockClient["publish"]`); the MockClient interface uses intersection with RealtimeClient.publish to preserve both the mock API and the function signature. (3) eslint `@typescript-eslint/no-non-null-assertion` errors on `res.body!` and `(await reader.read()).value!` test idioms — fixed by extracting two helper functions (`getBody(res)` and `readChunkRaw(reader)`) that throw on missing body / done state instead of asserting non-null.
- Errors resolved:     all (clean pass through TDD + acceptance gate; final state is typecheck 6/6 + lint 5/5 + 124 tests + build clean).
- Two-stage review:    Stage 1 PASS — Server foundation per the SSE-1 split plan: Valkey pub/sub publisher + subscriber + per-user SSE endpoint with manual auth + tenant + user scope + heartbeat + cleanup-on-cancel. Channel scheme locked. Alerts processor publishes AFTER tx commit. Best-effort delivery semantics documented in code comments. Every plan checklist item present. Stage 2 PASS — no new `any` in source; TDD order verified (RED→GREEN documented for each module); only scope files touched (3 new source files + 4 new test files + 2 modified source files + 1 package.json + 0 docs/schema = 10 files); conventional commit prefix `feat(realtime): SSE-1 foundation — Valkey pub/sub publisher + subscriber + per-user notification stream`. No observability instrumentation (matches SS-1/SS-2/SS-3/SS-4 surface — exports added none either; can revisit in SSE-3 hardening if needed). vercel-plugin "use Vercel Workflow" hook recommendation rejected (SSE streams are the intended Vercel Functions pattern, not durable jobs).
- Plan deviations:     none of substance. The original SSE-1 plan called for publishing INSIDE the $transaction; pulled to OUTSIDE the transaction at implementation time because publishing inside risks blocking the transaction commit on slow Redis writes, and best-effort delivery is the documented goal (clients reconcile via Last-Event-ID on reconnect). Added an explicit try/catch around the publish call to honor the "publisher failure does not roll back DB" invariant — this is also covered by a new test case in alerts.processor.test.ts.
- Branch:              feat/sse-foundation (clean linear commit from main HEAD 3aee3df; squash-merge to main pending user confirmation).
- Lessons:             🟤 decision — "Valkey pub/sub is the cross-process notification fan-out backbone for SSE. BullMQ workers (packages/jobs) and Next.js Route Handlers (apps/web) are separate processes; in-memory pub/sub does not span them. ioredis is already a transitive dep via BullMQ in packages/jobs, added as a direct dep to apps/web for the subscriber. Each SSE connection creates its own dedicated subscriber-mode ioredis connection — required because SUBSCRIBE blocks regular commands; the SSE cancel handler must call unsubscribe() + quit() to release the connection or the app leaks one TCP socket per cancelled stream. Channel naming locked: per-user channels for notifications (privacy), per-tenant broadcast for events feed (operators see all)." 🟢 change — "SSE-1 server foundation shipped — ioredis added to apps/web, publisher singleton lazy-constructed from REDIS_* env vars, per-user SSE endpoint at /api/stream/notifications. Best-effort delivery semantics: DB notification row is durable, SSE is fan-out. SSE-2 (client wrapper + React hook + sidebar polling replacement) and SSE-3 (events stream + War Room + security hardening + E2E) remaining. No new repo-wide 🔴 gotchas observed."

(2) Lint flagged 3 errors after first impl: `no-misused-spread` on `vi.importActual` spread (the actual @react-pdf/renderer exports include React components flagged as classes by the rule); `restrict-template-expressions` on `\`e${i}\`` where i is a number in the 10001-row fixture; `no-base-to-string` on `String(v: unknown)` in summarizeFilters because v could conceptually be an object that would stringify as `[object Object]`.

Lessons.md captures this as a 🟡 fix for SS-2/SS-3/SS-4 test authors. (2) Lint fixes: eslint-disable-next-line on the importActual spread with an explanatory comment (the React components Document/Page/Text/View/StyleSheet must remain functional for export-pdf.tsx's module-load even though only renderToBuffer is overridden as a stub); `\`e${String(i)}\`` for numeric template coercion; tightened summarizeFilters parameter type from `Record<string, unknown>` to `Record<string, string | number | undefined>` — the only call site passes the parsed Zod filter object (string enum + optional number) so the tighter type is accurate and removes the unsafe stringification path.

SS-2/3/4 will face the same reality: code is the single source of truth, mirror what the router accepts. (b) Plan suggested `<Link href={buildExportUrl(...)}>` for the UI buttons but Next.js's `<Link>` is for client-side navigation and `download` only fires on plain `<a>` tags — switched to `<Button asChild><a download href=...>` per the plan's own "Native `<a download href=...>` button — No JS download library needed" rationale a few lines later. (c) Foundation primitive `requireRouteAuth()` takes no `req` parameter (Auth.js v5 reads request context automatically) — already established in SS-0; route handler still receives `req: NextRequest` from the GET signature for URL parsing.

[]` on the always-defined `roles` field. - Plan deviations:     route-auth.ts signature changed from `requireRouteAuth(req: NextRequest)` (plan) to `requireRouteAuth()` (no parameter) — Auth.js v5's `auth()` reads the request via Next's headers/cookies context automatically, so the explicit `req` parameter is unnecessary and would force callers to pass a value they don't need. Callers in SS-1..4 will still receive `req` from the GET handler signature and use it for rate-limiter token extraction directly — the auth helper does not need it. Plan also said it would return `RouteAuthError` carrying a `Response`; implementation introduces a tiny `RouteAuthError` class wrapping `NextResponse` so callers can `catch (e) { if (e instanceof RouteAuthError) return e.response; throw e; }` — cleaner than throwing a bare `Response` since that breaks instanceof checks across runtimes.

## 2026-05-12 — Phase 8 Batch 2 Tier-1 cleanup: Seed passwords sourced from env vars (rotation-capable)
- Agent:               CLAUDE_CODE (Opus 4.7 direct execution — Tier 1 task, ~5 files, well under thrashing threshold)
- Why:                 Lifts the seed password gotcha tracked in STATE.md (next-1) and observation 292/391. Previous seed hardcoded `WEBMASTER_PASSWORD` as a top-level constant and used `update: {}` on the user upsert, so plaintext passwords lived in git history forever AND `pnpm db:seed` could never rotate the password on existing users. Same applied to the `DemoAdmin2024!SecurePass` literal for the demo site admin.
- Files added:         none
- Files modified:      packages/db/prisma/seed.ts (removed hardcoded WEBMASTER_PASSWORD constant and the `"DemoAdmin2024!SecurePass"` literal; added `requireEnv()` helper that throws with a remediation pointer when WEBMASTER_PASSWORD or DEMO_SITE_ADMIN_PASSWORD is unset; both bcrypt hashes computed once at top of main; both user upserts now use `update: { passwordHash }` instead of `update: {}` so re-seeding rotates), .env.dev / .env.staging / .env.prod (added WEBMASTER_PASSWORD + DEMO_SITE_ADMIN_PASSWORD per env — unique 22-char openssl-generated values per environment, never reused), .env.example (added matching placeholders), CREDENTIALS.md (rewrote First Admin Account section as a two-table layout: Webmaster + Demo Site Admin, both with per-env rows; added rotation procedure note pointing at env-file edit + re-seed).
- Files deleted:       none
- Schema/migrations:   none
- Tests:               typecheck clean (6 packages), lint clean (5 packages), 32/32 web router tests pass. Seed re-run against dev DB succeeded. Rotation verified by `bcrypt.compare(process.env.WEBMASTER_PASSWORD, user.passwordHash)` returning true post-seed for both accounts.
- Errors encountered:  none (clean Tier 1 task — Opus direct execution, no subagent dispatch needed)
- Errors resolved:     n/a

## 2026-05-12 — Phase 8 Batch 2 Item 2: Map patrol-area polygon overlays — MAP FEATURE GROUP COMPLETE
- Agent:               CLAUDE_CODE (Opus 4.7 direct execution — Sonnet bypassed per the thrashing lesson reproduced earlier this session, no subagent dispatch attempted)
- Why:                 Close out the Phase 8 Batch 2 map feature group by rendering Marine Protected Area (MPA) polygons on the operator map. Geo router `mapRouter.patrolAreas.list` already returned `polygonGeojson` + `colorHex` per area; this branch wires the UI consumer. mapcn primitive does NOT expose a polygon component, so a new `MapPolygon` wrapper encapsulates the imperative MapLibre dance.
- Files added:         apps/web/src/components/map/MapPolygon.tsx (119 lines — client component using `useMap()` from mapcn to imperatively `map.addSource({ type: "geojson", data: { type: "Feature", geometry: polygonGeojson } })` + two `map.addLayer` calls (one `type: "fill"` for the area, one `type: "line"` for the outline). Three useEffect hooks: setup on mount, data update on geojson change, paint update on color/opacity change. Cleanup on unmount via removeLayer + removeSource wrapped in try/catch — mapcn may unmount the map first. Props: `geojson: GeoJSON.Polygon | GeoJSON.MultiPolygon`, `color: string`, optional `fillOpacity` (default 0.2), `outlineOpacity` (default 0.8), `outlineWidth` (default 1.5).)
- Files modified:      apps/web/src/components/map/InteractiveMap.tsx (added `trpc.map.patrolAreas.list.useQuery({ activeOnly: true })`, rendered `<MapPolygon>` for each result inside `<Map>` BEFORE `<MapRoute>` so the polygon fill stays under the patrol track line in z-order. Type-cast `area.polygonGeojson` through `unknown` to satisfy Prisma's `JsonValue` → `GeoJSON.Polygon | GeoJSON.MultiPolygon` narrowing.)
- Files deleted:       none
- Schema/migrations:   none (read-only consumption of existing `mapRouter.patrolAreas.list`).
- Tests:               32/32 web router tests pass — `patrolAreas.list` was already covered by 2 of the 10 map router tests (sub-session 1.1). Typecheck clean. Lint clean.
- Errors encountered:  (1) First typecheck pass failed with `TS2352: Conversion of type 'JsonValue' to type 'Polygon | MultiPolygon' may be a mistake` — Prisma's `Json` type is a discriminated union that needs explicit `unknown` intermediate cast. (2) First lint pass flagged two errors in MapPolygon: `react-hooks/exhaustive-deps` rule disable comment for a rule the project doesn't have configured (the comment itself was invalid), and an unnecessary type assertion on the `map.getSource()` return.
- Errors resolved:     (1) Changed cast to `area.polygonGeojson as unknown as GeoJSON.Polygon | GeoJSON.MultiPolygon`. The cast is honest — Prisma stores GeoJSON in a Json column at runtime; the type system needs the narrowing. (2) Removed the disable comment (project doesn't enforce exhaustive-deps so the omission is fine) and moved the type assertion inline to the `setData` call site where it's actually needed.
- Two-stage review:    Stage 1 PASS — polygons render per area with correct color, both fill and outline visible. Stage 2 PASS — no any types, MapPolygon mirrors the MapRoute pattern (idempotent setup, data-update effect, paint-update effect, cleanup), only 2 blast-radius files touched, conventional commit.
- Branch:              feat/map-patrol-areas → squash-merged to main as `7250039`. Branch deleted.
- Map feature group:   COMPLETE — tile basemap (1.2c) + subjects markers (f041215) + events markers (f041215) + patrol tracks (e1e2d8a) + patrol areas (7250039). All four data layers from `mapRouter` now have UI consumers. PRODUCT.md L191 "Geospatial Operator View" requirement is fully satisfied.

## 2026-06-12 — Bug #6: super_admin null-tenant layout redirect (Swarm S2)
- Agent:               CLAUDE_CODE (Opus 4.8 — swarm worker S2, branch swarm/phase7-per-area-report-flip)
- Why:                 super_admins have no home tenant — the Auth.js session callback normalizes their null DB tenantId to "" (auth/config.ts L102). Without a gate, navigating to any (dashboard) route rendered tenant-scoped pages with no tenant context (empty/broken UI). The (dashboard) layout now redirects them to the /admin platform console (shipped Item 1, e5cd29d) before any tenant-scoped child renders. Pure UX gate — no tenant routers touched.
- Files added:         apps/web/src/app/(dashboard)/__tests__/layout.test.tsx (3 vitest cases — redirect on super_admin+empty-tenant+no-cookie; NO redirect while impersonating; NO redirect for regular tenant user)
- Files modified:      apps/web/src/app/(dashboard)/layout.tsx (converted to async server component; calls auth() + redirect("/admin") for super_admin with session.tenantId === ""), docs/CHANGELOG_AI.md, .cline/STATE.md
- Files deleted:       none
- Schema/migrations:   none
- Errors encountered:  Next.js production build (Phase 7 V31.4 gate) flagged @typescript-eslint/strict-boolean-expressions on `session?.user.roles.includes(...)` — optional chaining made the conditional a nullable boolean.
- Errors resolved:     Replaced the optional-chain with an explicit `session !== null &&` guard (matches route-auth.ts style). Build re-ran clean.
- Design note:         The gate is impersonation-aware. Item 4 (commit c20190e/aa8fbef) lets a super_admin browse a tenant's dashboard via the HttpOnly `mg-impersonate-tenant` cookie while session.tenantId stays "". An impersonation-blind redirect would have regressed that shipped flow, so the layout reads the cookie via next/headers and skips the redirect when parseImpersonationCookieFromHeader() returns a valid tenant id — mirroring requireRouteAuth() in server/lib/route-auth.ts. The scope's conceptual `tenantId == null` maps to the codebase's real `=== ""` session sentinel (== null never matches post-normalization).
- Verification:        Phase 7 hard pre-merge gate — all 4 commands GREEN: pnpm tools:check-product-sync ✓ (5 docs, no private tags), pnpm typecheck ✓ (7/7 packages), pnpm test ✓ (737 web vitest, +3 new), pnpm --filter @marine-guardian/web build ✓ (Next.js production build, ESLint clean after the strict-boolean fix).
- Final ship:          Single feat(phase-4-S2) commit on branch swarm/phase7-per-area-report-flip. NO origin push (human reviews and pushes).
